## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration is governed by restoring forces (functions of x) and possibly damping forces (functions of v), characteristic of nonlinear dynamical systems in classical mechanics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with damping)
- Van der Pol-like oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with periodic forcing)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (combined linear and cubic damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force for large-angle oscillations)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- General polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (quadratic and cubic nonlinearities)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in position (x**2) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Velocity-dependent terms (v, v**3) → energy dissipation or injection (damping or self-excitation)
- Position-velocity coupling (x**2 * v) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type dynamics
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- Negative linear damping with positive cubic damping (c1*v + c2*v**3 with opposite signs) → limit cycle behavior
- sin(c*x) restoring force → pendulum-like dynamics with multiple equilibria
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system (conservative or dissipative without external drive)

Wait — can `v*sin(x)` generate a `v` component? No. So we need an explicit `v` term.

**Candidate 4:** `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*sin(t) - v*sin(c3*x + c4)`
Expand: `-v*sin(c3*x+c4) = -v[sin(c3*x)cos(c4) + cos(c3*x)sin(c4)]`. Set c3=1: `-cos(c4)*v*sin(x) - sin(c4)*v*cos(x)`. This gives `v*sin(x)` and `v*cos(x)` but NOT standalone `v`. Set c1=0. Missing `v` term. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x + c1*v*(x²-1) + c2*sin(t) + c3*log(c4*v+1) + c5*v*sin(c6*x + c7)`
The log term can't produce linear `v`. The `v*(x²-1)` gives `v*x² - v`. Set c1 for the `-v` part, but adds unwanted `v*x²`. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 9:** `c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*v + c3*v³ + c4*v*x² + c5*v*sin(c6*x + c7)`
Set c3=0, c4=0, c6=1, c7=0: `c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*v + c5*v*sin(x)`. This matches! **[MATCH]**

**Candidate 10:** `c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*v*sin(c3*x + c4) + c5*v + c6*v³`
Set c6=0, c3=1, c4=0: `c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*v*sin(x) + c5*v`. **[MATCH]**

**Candidate 11:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(t) + c3*v*x² + c4*v*sin(c5*x + c6)`
Set c3=0, c5=1, c6=0: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(t) + c4*v*sin(x)`. **[MATCH]**
